     ╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
     │ Plugins declare interfaces; drivers implement them                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Context                                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Arche's archetype/ECS model has one underlying problem wearing several  │
     │ hats: how do a library and the program that uses it share definitional  │
     │ vocabulary — shapes, components/types, and the storage (pools) for them │
     │ — when the program, not the library, must have the ultimate say, and    │
     │ the two cannot be edited together?                                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The original WORLDS_PLAN.md answered with first-class world values,     │
     │ run/insert/delete … in W, world structs/registries/GEPs, and a          │
     │ @cfg(<slug>) conditional-compilation attribute. A long design pass      │
     │ discarded almost all of it for a single spine:                          │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Everything is a plugin or a driver — groups all the way up: files →     │
     │ plugin → driver.                                                        │
     │ - A plugin (library) is a group of files: an .i.arche interface file    │
     │ declaring the vocabulary it requires, plus system files providing       │
     │ behavior and a doctest driver. It owns no canonical definitions and no  │
     │ storage, so two plugins can never collide.                              │
     │ - A driver (the program/consumer) is a group of plugins: it owns the    │
     │ canonical definitions and storage, and binds its own vocabulary to each │
     │ plugin's requirements per-decl (bar :: int implements physics.foo),     │
     │ sizes pools, and runs systems. The top-level program is a driver; a     │
     │ module can also drive its own sub-plugins.                              │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Why this shape (each point decided during design, grounded in code):    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1. Storage is already canonical-shape-keyed and scope-independent.      │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl / canonical_arch_name (codegen.c:1031-1062)    │
     │ make a name an alias for a shape; get_arch_static_capacity              │
     │ (codegen.c:1065) canonicalizes both sides. No worlds/in W/GEP machinery │
     │ — the only storage gap is naming a shape that lives in another module.  │
     │ 2. @cfg is the wrong primitive — a per-decl attribute clashing with the │
     │ "everything is a group/region" architecture                             │
     │ (#import/#module/#file/#foreign). Its only motivation, test             │
     │ scaffolding, is better served by doctests.                              │
     │ 3. Test scaffolding is already a group: the in-file doctest driver.     │
     │ synthesize() (doctest_run.c:78) prepends the file's entire source and   │
     │ splices an example with its own main at top level (doctest_run.c:84);   │
     │ doctests run only under arche test (cli/cmd_test.c:33), never under     │
     │ arche build. A plugin cannot be tested as a plugin — testing it means   │
     │ implementing it, so a plugin's doctest is a driver: it defines the      │
     │ canonical types that satisfy the plugin's interface (its .i.arche       │
     │ requirements), binds them with implements clauses, sizes the pools, and │
     │ drives the systems. The doctest is just the smallest possible driver,   │
     │ excluded from any real driver's build.                                  │
     │ 4. Conflicts must be fixable, so plugins own no canonical definitions.  │
     │ A lib-vs-lib clash (two DLLs both defining bar :: int differently) is   │
     │ unfixable by the consumer, so it must never arise. Plugins declare      │
     │ requirements; the driver owns canonical defs and the bindings; every    │
     │ error surfaces at the driver, where the consumer can act.               │
     │ 5. Shape/field identity is name-based, and that is correct. bar :: int  │
     │ and baz :: int mean different things; you cannot auto-merge by type     │
     │ without merging health and score. Divergence is resolved not by         │
     │ inference but by the driver's explicit binding: it maps each plugin's   │
     │ required name onto one canonical component (foo := bar, baz := bar),    │
     │ type-checked at the binding. Names need not coincide across plugins.    │
     │ 6. Private/internal types stay private by default. A plugin's internal  │
     │ types are normal decls, namespaced to their #module/#file region        │
     │ (lib.Scratch via prefixed_dup), never surfaced and never collidable.    │
     │ Only what a plugin lists in its .i.arche interface file is              │
     │ shared/driver-owned vocabulary. The global-canonical behavior is opt-in │
     │ (the interface), not the default.                                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The plugin/driver mechanism (interface file + per-decl implements)      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Groups all the way up: files → plugin → driver. A plugin is a group of  │
     │ files (an .i.arche interface file + system files + a doctest driver); a │
     │ driver is a group of plugins it imports and implements.                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/physics.i.arche  — INTERFACE FILE: every decl is a           │
     │ requirement (role carried by .i.arche name)                             │
     │ foo :: int                         // a component the driver must own   │
     │ Particle :: archetype { pos, foo } // a shape the driver must provide   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/systems.arche     — plugin behavior + private decls          │
     │ Scratch :: archetype { tmp }       // private/internal — namespaced,    │
     │ never surfaced                                                          │
     │ integrate :: sys { /* uses Particle, foo */ }                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // driver — a group of plugins; owns canonical defs; binds per-decl     │
     │ (one decl, many plugins)                                                │
     │ #import { physics, render }                                             │
     │ bar   :: int                       implements physics.foo               │
     │    // type-checked: int ~ int                                           │
     │ Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }    implements physics.Particle,         │
     │ render.Sprite                                                           │
     │ run physics.integrate;             // runs against Thing via the        │
     │ binding                                                                 │
     │ run render.draw;                                                        │
     │ - The interface is a file, not a region: a *.i.arche file in the plugin │
     │ folder; every decl in it is a requirement the driver must satisfy. No   │
     │ in-content marker — the filename carries the role, consistent with      │
     │ Arche already naming file roles (core.arche, test_*.arche) and          │
     │ discovering modules by glob.                                            │
     │ - The binding is a per-decl implements <plugin>.<req>, … clause         │
     │ carrying a comma list / repeatable target set, so one driver type       │
     │ implements many plugins at once (Thing above satisfies both             │
     │ physics.Particle and render.Sprite). "bar implements foo" is inherently │
     │ per-declaration.                                                        │
     │ - A requirement is typed but name-mapped, not name-matched — the        │
     │ interface carries enough type to check the bind; the driver supplies    │
     │ the name correspondence.                                                │
     │ - #foreign is the existing precedent (it declares functions a lib       │
     │ requires externally); the .i.arche interface rotates that onto          │
     │ types/shapes.                                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Standing constraints                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - NEVER move anything to known_failures unless explicitly told. Never   │
     │ touch git. Run make format before tests. Tests under tests/, never      │
     │ tmp/. One test at a time; negative tests for bugs.                      │
     │ - Regression gate: tests/unit/language/systems/ must stay green.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 1 — Ready to build: caller-sized pools + literal unification       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Concrete, file-level, independent — the first deliverables of the       │
     │ spine; they stand regardless of how the interface regions land.         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1a. Qualified pool decls (driver sizes an imported shape)               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Syntax: lib.Particle[1000] (full [C](N){V} grammar), naming an        │
     │ imported shape.                                                         │
     │ - Back end already handles it: import renames a shape to the dotted     │
     │ canonical identity lib.Particle (lower.c prefixed_dup, "%s.%s"); a pool │
     │ decl whose archetype_name is "lib.Particle" resolves via                │
     │ canonical_arch_name and sizes its one global — no codegen change on the │
     │ happy path.                                                             │
     │ - Gap: parse_static_decl (parser.c:757-803) consumes one bare IDENT     │
     │ (line 760) then expects [; lib.Particle[N] bails at the ..              │
     │ - Changes: (1) parser accepts an optional .IDENT chain after the        │
     │ leading IDENT, recording the joined name; (2) lowering carries the      │
     │ dotted name verbatim into archetype_name (confirm hir_q_decl,           │
     │ lower.c:2563, needs no rewrite — it already equals the canonical        │
     │ identity); (3) no-silent-conflict diagnostic in                         │
     │ get_arch_static_capacity (codegen.c:1065) when two pool decls resolve   │
     │ to one canonical shape.                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1b. Anonymous shape literals unify with named shapes                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Goal: arche { foo, bar } lowers to the same canonical shape as a      │
     │ named Foo :: arche { foo, bar }.                                        │
     │ - Current: literals parse (SN_ARCH_EXPR, parser.c:1170); in a binding   │
     │ they lower via lower_archetype_from (lower.c:1666), but an anonymous    │
     │ one in expression position falls through to a placeholder               │
     │ (lower.c:770-775) and never reaches canonical_archetype_decl.           │
     │ - Change: replace the fallthrough so an anonymous SN_ARCH_EXPR mints a  │
     │ synthetic HirArchetypeDecl (deterministic name from the sorted          │
     │ field-name set, so identical literals dedupe), registers it in the      │
     │ program decls, and yields a shape reference — existing field-name       │
     │ canonicalization then folds it onto any structurally-identical named    │
     │ shape. No identity-rule change.                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 2 — Design-stage: the plugin/driver interface system               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Interface declaration form is decided: the interface file convention    │
     │ (Option B) — chosen for the "groups all the way up" model and for       │
     │ discoverability. Rationale grounded in code: Arche already encodes file │
     │ role by name (core.arche special-cased by inode, compile.c:241-247;     │
     │ test_*.arche convention) and discovers modules by globbing *.arche      │
     │ (try_load_module_dir) rather than parsing for role; multi-file modules  │
     │ already merge, so one .i.arche file gives a single canonical contract;  │
     │ and globbing *.i.arche makes arche init driver/IDE discovery O(1). No   │
     │ #requires region is added.                                              │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Policy settled (above); mechanics need a focused detailing pass before  │
     │ coding. Captured with code touchpoints:                                 │
     │ - Interface file *.i.arche (plugin): extend the module loader           │
     │ (try_load_module_dir / register_module_file, compile.c:114-162) to      │
     │ recognize *.i.arche files in a plugin folder and register their decls   │
     │ separately, marked "required, not owned" (bodiless/typed entries —      │
     │ components foo :: int, shapes Particle :: archetype { … }). No new      │
     │ parser syntax; the filename is the marker. Validate that a driver does  │
     │ not re-own a required name except via an implements bind.               │
     │ - implements <plugin>.<req>, … clause (driver): a per-decl binding tail │
     │ on the driver's own canonical decl (comma list → one decl, many         │
     │ plugins), type-checked at the bind. Parser: accept an optional          │
     │ implements <qualified-name>{, <qualified-name>} tail on a decl. It      │
     │ produces a per-plugin name-substitution applied when the plugin's       │
     │ systems/shapes are lowered into the driver — conceptually an extension  │
     │ of the module qualify/rename pass (hir_q_decl/hir_rn_decl,              │
     │ lower.c:2320-2563), which already rewrites cross-module names; here it  │
     │ rewrites required names → bound canonical names.                        │
     │ - Private-by-default: unchanged module prefixing; only .i.arche         │
     │ interface entries are shared. No change to existing decls.              │
     │ - Doctest-for-interfaces: a plugin's doctest is a driver — it must      │
     │ define canonical types satisfying the plugin's interface, bind them     │
     │ with implements clauses, size the pools, and drive the systems.         │
     │ synthesize() already splices the example at top level verbatim, so      │
     │ implements-clause decls and pool decls are valid there; confirm the     │
     │ loader makes the plugin's own .i.arche requirements visible to its      │
     │ doctest. No "test a plugin without implementing it" path exists.        │
     │ - Unsatisfied/incompatible requirements → driver-side error (reuse the  │
     │ sem diagnostic table), naming the requirement and the plugin — always   │
     │ fixable in the driver.                                                  │
     │ - Entry point: the tuple-group registry is the half-built version of    │
     │ shared vocabulary — g_tgroups[64] (lower.c:1320) is already             │
     │ global/bare-name/unprefixed but lacks conflict handling, cross-module   │
     │ registration (build_tgroups, lower.c:1391, scans only the root), and    │
     │ caps at 64 (register_tgroup, lower.c:1327). It folds into the component │
     │ side of the interface/implements system.                                │
     │ - Before coding Part 2: write a follow-up pinning the .i.arche          │
     │ interface entry rules, the implements-clause binding/substitution       │
     │ lowering, the component-vs-named-type boundary, same-name auto-bind vs  │
     │ always-explicit, and how a plugin typechecks when built only in a       │
     │ driver's context.                                                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 3 — Tooling: arche init (driver/plugin scaffolding)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The interface being machine-readable is what makes scaffolding cheap,   │
     │ and it operationalizes "what must I define to use this lib." A new CLI  │
     │ command beside cmd_test/cmd_build (cli/cmd_init.c, registered like the  │
     │ others):                                                                │
     │ - arche init driver <plugin> — read the plugin's interface, emit a      │
     │ driver skeleton: stub canonical defs for each required component/shape, │
     │ an implements <plugin>.<req> clause on each, pool-size stubs, and a     │
     │ main that calls the plugin's systems. The generated driver is the       │
     │ consumer's starting point.                                              │
     │ - arche init plugin <name> — scaffold a plugin folder: an interface     │
     │ declaration, a systems file, and a doctest driver stub that implements  │
     │ the interface for arche test.                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Depends on Part 2's interface grammar; lands after it.                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 4 — Documentation (the plugin/driver philosophy is first-class)    │

     │ driver; groups all the way up (files → plugin → driver)." Covers: a     │
     │ plugin is a group of files (.i.arche interface + systems + doctest      │
     │ driver) that owns no canonical defs/storage; a driver is a group of     │

     │ - docs/language.md — sections for the .i.arche interface-file role, the │

     │ - docs/tooling.md — arche init driver <plugin> / arche init plugin      │

     │ plugin, implement it in a driver, test via doctest); docs/DOCTESTS.md — │
     │ the doctest-as-driver framing.                                          │
     │ - README.md — a short pointer to docs/plugins.md as a headline design   │
     │ idea. Retire/redirect WORLDS_PLAN.md (superseded by this plan).         │

● You want a real exploration of the binding syntax. Let me put a subagent on
  it.

● Explore(Explore implements binding syntax)
  ⎿  Done (33 tool uses · 41.7k tokens · 2m 0s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

● The subagent's exploration is in. First, a clarifying reframe that simplifies
  the whole thing: in any per-decl form, the declaration is the local name, so
  Thing :: archetype {…} implements physics.Particle unambiguously means "Thing
  ↔ Particle" — no as/= remapping needed in the common case (the subagent
  over-worried about this). The real fork is where the binding lives:

  Per-decl — binding sits on the decl (two surface forms):
  // A. tail clause (current plan)
  Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }  implements physics.Particle, render.Sprite

  // C. decorator (subagent's pick)
  @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)
  Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }
  Both keep a type's bindings on the type, make "one type → many plugins"
  trivial (a comma list), and have no one-per-file limit. The decorator (C) is
  the subagent's recommendation because Arche already parses stacked decorators
  (@allow(…), @drop(…), parser.c:944-1013) — so it's the cheapest to add and the
  most idiomatic, clustering at the decl head exactly like the existing ones.

  Grouped per-plugin — binding collected by plugin (your lib impl sketch,
  Pattern B):
  #physics impl
  Particle = Thing
  foo = bar

  #render impl
  Sprite = Thing
  This reads well for bulk binding and makes the req = local mapping explicit,
  but it has two real problems the subagent flagged: banner regions are
  EOF-sticky → one plugin per file, and it scatters a multi-plugin type's 
  bindings (your Thing appears under both #physics impl and #render impl,
  possibly in different files) — which fights directly against "one driver type
  implements multiple plugins."

  Separate .impl.arche file (Pattern D): maximal separation and very "groups,"
  but two files to keep in sync and weak locality — better suited to
  machine-generated drivers than hand-written ones.

  The subagent's verdict: decorator @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)
  as the primary, since it's the most idiomatic (reuses the decorator
  machinery), keeps bindings local to the type, handles multi-plugin trivially,
  and arche init can emit it cleanly. The grouped #plugin impl form stays
  available as a secondary for bulk binding if you want it.

  My read agrees: decorator is the best fit — it's literally the shape of
  Arche's existing @allow/@drop, and it's the only per-decl-grouped option that
  doesn't fight the multi-plugin requirement. But the grouped form is genuinely
  closer to your "everything is a group" instinct, at the cost of the
  one-plugin-per-file limit.

  Which do you want as the binding syntax — the @implements(...) decorator, the
  … implements ... tail clause, the grouped #plugin impl form, or
  decorator-primary with the grouped form as a bulk alternative? Once you pick,
  I'll lock it into the plan.

✻ Sautéed for 6m 43s

     ╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
     │ Plugins declare interfaces; drivers implement them                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Context                                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Arche's archetype/ECS model has one underlying problem wearing several  │
     │ hats: how do a library and the program that uses it share definitional  │
     │ vocabulary — shapes, components/types, and the storage (pools) for them │
     │ — when the program, not the library, must have the ultimate say, and    │
     │ the two cannot be edited together?                                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The original WORLDS_PLAN.md answered with first-class world values,     │
     │ run/insert/delete … in W, world structs/registries/GEPs, and a          │
     │ @cfg(<slug>) conditional-compilation attribute. A long design pass      │
     │ discarded almost all of it for a single spine:                          │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Everything is a plugin or a driver — groups all the way up: files →     │
     │ plugin → driver.                                                        │
     │ - A plugin (library) is a group of files: an .i.arche interface file    │
     │ declaring the vocabulary it requires, plus system files providing       │
     │ behavior and a doctest driver. It owns no canonical definitions and no  │
     │ storage, so two plugins can never collide.                              │
     │ - A driver (the program/consumer) is a group of plugins: it owns the    │
     │ canonical definitions and storage, and binds its own vocabulary to each │
     │ plugin's requirements with an @implements(...) decorator                │
     │ (@implements(physics.foo) bar :: int), sizes pools, and runs systems.   │
     │ The top-level program is a driver; a module can also drive its own      │
     │ sub-plugins.                                                            │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Why this shape (each point decided during design, grounded in code):    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1. Storage is already canonical-shape-keyed and scope-independent.      │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl / canonical_arch_name (codegen.c:1031-1062)    │
     │ make a name an alias for a shape; get_arch_static_capacity              │
     │ (codegen.c:1065) canonicalizes both sides. No worlds/in W/GEP machinery │
     │ — the only storage gap is naming a shape that lives in another module.  │
     │ 2. @cfg is the wrong primitive — a per-decl attribute clashing with the │
     │ "everything is a group/region" architecture                             │
     │ (#import/#module/#file/#foreign). Its only motivation, test             │
     │ scaffolding, is better served by doctests.                              │
     │ 3. Test scaffolding is already a group: the in-file doctest driver.     │
     │ synthesize() (doctest_run.c:78) prepends the file's entire source and   │
     │ splices an example with its own main at top level (doctest_run.c:84);   │
     │ doctests run only under arche test (cli/cmd_test.c:33), never under     │
     │ arche build. A plugin cannot be tested as a plugin — testing it means   │
     │ implementing it, so a plugin's doctest is a driver: it defines the      │
     │ canonical types that satisfy the plugin's interface (its .i.arche       │
     │ requirements), binds them with @implements(...) decorators, sizes the   │
     │ pools, and drives the systems. The doctest is just the smallest         │
     │ possible driver, excluded from any real driver's build.                 │
     │ 4. Conflicts must be fixable, so plugins own no canonical definitions.  │
     │ A lib-vs-lib clash (two DLLs both defining bar :: int differently) is   │
     │ unfixable by the consumer, so it must never arise. Plugins declare      │
     │ requirements; the driver owns canonical defs and the bindings; every    │
     │ error surfaces at the driver, where the consumer can act.               │
     │ 5. Shape/field identity is name-based, and that is correct. bar :: int  │
     │ and baz :: int mean different things; you cannot auto-merge by type     │
     │ without merging health and score. Divergence is resolved not by         │
     │ inference but by the driver's explicit binding: it maps each plugin's   │
     │ required name onto one canonical component (foo := bar, baz := bar),    │
     │ type-checked at the binding. Names need not coincide across plugins.    │
     │ 6. Private/internal types stay private by default. A plugin's internal  │
     │ types are normal decls, namespaced to their #module/#file region        │
     │ (lib.Scratch via prefixed_dup), never surfaced and never collidable.    │
     │ Only what a plugin lists in its .i.arche interface file is              │
     │ shared/driver-owned vocabulary. The global-canonical behavior is opt-in │
     │ (the interface), not the default.                                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The plugin/driver mechanism (interface file + @implements decorator)    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Groups all the way up: files → plugin → driver. A plugin is a group of  │
     │ files (an .i.arche interface file + system files + a doctest driver); a │
     │ driver is a group of plugins it imports and implements.                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/physics.i.arche  — INTERFACE FILE: every decl is a           │
     │ requirement (role carried by .i.arche name)                             │
     │ foo :: int                         // a component the driver must own   │
     │ Particle :: archetype { pos, foo } // a shape the driver must provide   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/systems.arche     — plugin behavior + private decls          │
     │ Scratch :: archetype { tmp }       // private/internal — namespaced,    │
     │ never surfaced                                                          │
     │ integrate :: sys { /* uses Particle, foo */ }                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // driver — a group of plugins; owns canonical defs; binds with         │
     │ @implements (one decl, many plugins)                                    │
     │ #import { physics, render }                                             │
     │ @implements(physics.foo)                                                │
     │ bar :: int                                       // type-checked: int ~ │
     │ int                                                                     │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)                            │
     │ Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }                  // one decl satisfies  │
     │ two plugins                                                             │
     │ run physics.integrate;                           // runs against Thing  │
     │ via the binding                                                         │
     │ run render.draw;                                                        │
     │ - The interface is a file, not a region: a *.i.arche file in the plugin │
     │ folder; every decl in it is a requirement the driver must satisfy. No   │
     │ in-content marker — the filename carries the role, consistent with      │
     │ Arche already naming file roles (core.arche, test_*.arche) and          │
     │ discovering modules by glob.                                            │
     │ - The binding is a stacked / comma-list @implements(<plugin>.<req>, …)  │
     │ decorator on the driver's decl, reusing Arche's existing decorator      │
     │ machinery (@allow/@drop, parser.c:944-1013). The decl is the local      │
     │ side, so @implements(physics.Particle) on Thing means Thing↔Particle —  │
     │ no remap syntax needed. The comma list means one driver type implements │
     │ many plugins at once (Thing satisfies both physics.Particle and         │
     │ render.Sprite).                                                         │
     │ - A requirement is typed but name-mapped, not name-matched — the        │
     │ interface carries enough type to check the bind; the driver supplies    │
     │ the name correspondence.                                                │
     │ - #foreign is the existing precedent (it declares functions a lib       │
     │ requires externally); the .i.arche interface rotates that onto          │
     │ types/shapes.                                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Standing constraints                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - NEVER move anything to known_failures unless explicitly told. Never   │
     │ touch git. Run make format before tests. Tests under tests/, never      │
     │ tmp/. One test at a time; negative tests for bugs.                      │
     │ - Regression gate: tests/unit/language/systems/ must stay green.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 1 — Ready to build: caller-sized pools + literal unification       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Concrete, file-level, independent — the first deliverables of the       │
     │ spine; they stand regardless of how the interface regions land.         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1a. Qualified pool decls (driver sizes an imported shape)               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Syntax: lib.Particle[1000] (full [C](N){V} grammar), naming an        │
     │ imported shape.                                                         │
     │ - Back end already handles it: import renames a shape to the dotted     │
     │ canonical identity lib.Particle (lower.c prefixed_dup, "%s.%s"); a pool │
     │ decl whose archetype_name is "lib.Particle" resolves via                │
     │ canonical_arch_name and sizes its one global — no codegen change on the │
     │ happy path.                                                             │
     │ - Gap: parse_static_decl (parser.c:757-803) consumes one bare IDENT     │
     │ (line 760) then expects [; lib.Particle[N] bails at the ..              │
     │ - Changes: (1) parser accepts an optional .IDENT chain after the        │
     │ leading IDENT, recording the joined name; (2) lowering carries the      │
     │ dotted name verbatim into archetype_name (confirm hir_q_decl,           │
     │ lower.c:2563, needs no rewrite — it already equals the canonical        │
     │ identity); (3) no-silent-conflict diagnostic in                         │
     │ get_arch_static_capacity (codegen.c:1065) when two pool decls resolve   │
     │ to one canonical shape.                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1b. Anonymous shape literals unify with named shapes                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Goal: arche { foo, bar } lowers to the same canonical shape as a      │
     │ named Foo :: arche { foo, bar }.                                        │
     │ - Current: literals parse (SN_ARCH_EXPR, parser.c:1170); in a binding   │
     │ they lower via lower_archetype_from (lower.c:1666), but an anonymous    │
     │ one in expression position falls through to a placeholder               │
     │ (lower.c:770-775) and never reaches canonical_archetype_decl.           │
     │ - Change: replace the fallthrough so an anonymous SN_ARCH_EXPR mints a  │
     │ synthetic HirArchetypeDecl (deterministic name from the sorted          │
     │ field-name set, so identical literals dedupe), registers it in the      │
     │ program decls, and yields a shape reference — existing field-name       │
     │ canonicalization then folds it onto any structurally-identical named    │
     │ shape. No identity-rule change.                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 2 — Design-stage: the plugin/driver interface system               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Interface declaration form is decided: the interface file convention    │
     │ (Option B) — chosen for the "groups all the way up" model and for       │
     │ discoverability. Rationale grounded in code: Arche already encodes file │
     │ role by name (core.arche special-cased by inode, compile.c:241-247;     │
     │ test_*.arche convention) and discovers modules by globbing *.arche      │
     │ (try_load_module_dir) rather than parsing for role; multi-file modules  │
     │ already merge, so one .i.arche file gives a single canonical contract;  │
     │ and globbing *.i.arche makes arche init driver/IDE discovery O(1). No   │
     │ #requires region is added.                                              │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Policy settled (above); mechanics need a focused detailing pass before  │

● Good catch — that line is genuinely contradictory, and it exposes a
  terminology decision we haven't pinned. Let me answer the question directly,
  fix the line, and surface the real fork.

  Is "module" replaced by "plugin"? Yes — conceptually. In the user-facing model
  the unit is the plugin (a group of files that declares an interface) and the
  composing root is the driver. "Module" survives only as the implementation 
  mechanism — #import, the folder loader, g_modules, the lib.x prefixing — not
  as a concept we teach. So that line shouldn't say "module" at all.

  But fixing the word exposes a real model fork I'd baked in implicitly with "a
  module can also drive its own sub-plugins":

  - M1 — strict (one driver, at the root). A plugin owns nothing canonical; it
  only forwards requirements upward. A plugin that depends on another plugin
  re-exposes that plugin's unsatisfied requirements as part of its own
  interface, so the single root driver satisfies the whole transitive set in one
  canonical place. This keeps the no-conflict guarantee airtight ("plugins own
  nothing → plugins can't collide") and there is exactly one canonical
  vocabulary, at the root.
  - M2 — recursive (roles are relative). Every node drives the plugins below it
  (owns canonical defs to satisfy them) and exposes its remaining interface
  upward — so a node is a plugin to its parent and a driver to its children.
  More encapsulating (a plugin can bundle and satisfy its own dependencies),
  which is what "drive its own sub-plugins" implied. But it weakens "plugins own
  nothing canonical" for intermediate nodes, and reintroduces per-driver
  storage multiplicity (two intermediates that each satisfy the same sub-plugin
  → two canonical instances — the old worlds question, through the back door).

  The contradiction you spotted is M2-thinking written in M1-wording. They're
  both coherent; M1 is simpler and protects the conflict guarantee, M2 is more
  powerful but pulls storage multiplicity back in.

  I've changed the plan line to not say "module," and I'll record whichever
  model you pick:

● Updated plan
  ⎿  /plan to preview

● The line now reads correctly and flags the open decision.

  My lean is M1 (strict) — it keeps the property that made this whole design
  click for you (plugins own nothing, so two libs can never collide and every
  conflict is fixable at the root), and it avoids quietly resurrecting the
  per-world storage-multiplicity problem we spent this whole conversation
  removing. Requirement-forwarding can be automatic: a plugin's effective
  interface = its own .i.arche requirements plus any unsatisfied requirements of
  the plugins it imports, all bubbling up to the one root driver.

  M2 is worth it only if you specifically want a plugin to be able to bundle and
  satisfy its own dependencies (ship as a self-contained unit) — at the cost of
  that storage multiplicity.

  Which model do you want — M1 (one root driver, plugins forward) or M2 
  (recursive, every node drives its children)?

● Both decisions noted. Let me lock M1-for-now and engage the private-archetype
  question, because it turns out to be more load-bearing than it looks.

  M1 now, M2 later — and your instinct is right: M2 (encapsulated
  modules-with-drivers) most likely falls out of private scopes + private
  archetypes rather than needing a separate mechanism. A #file/#plugin region is
  already a private world; "having a driver in there" is just owning private
  canonical defs + bindings that don't leak. So we build M1 now but don't design
  anything that precludes that later. Let me record that.

● Updated plan
  ⎿  /plan to preview

● Now the real one — private archetypes. You're circling something important,
  and there's a concrete bug hiding under it.

  The risk, today: archetype identity is global and structural —
  canonical_archetype_decl (codegen.c:1031) unifies any two archetypes with the
  same field-name set, across the whole program, and import does not prefix
  field names (only the archetype's own name and field types get renamed,
  hir_rn_decl lower.c:2320). So if plugin A has an internal Cache { key, val }
  and plugin B independently has Cache { key, val }, importing both makes them
  silently share one canonical pool. That's a hidden coupling bug — and the
  plugin model makes it far more likely, because you're now composing many
  independently-authored plugins that never agreed to share storage.

  So "should we allow private archetypes?" is really "should internal shapes be
  protected from accidental cross-plugin unification?" — and I think the answer
  is yes, necessarily. It draws the exact same line the whole design rests on:

  - Public / interface shapes (the driver's canonical vocabulary, the .i.arche
  requirements) unify structurally and globally — that's the feature.
  - Private shapes (declared in a #file/#plugin private scope) are encapsulated
  — they unify only within their own scope, never across plugins. Plugin A's
  Cache and plugin B's Cache stay distinct, distinct pools.

  That's the public=structural / private=scoped boundary, which is just
  interface-vs-implementation again. And it's exactly the substrate your M2
  future wants — a #file/#plugin with private shapes + private pools + private
  bindings is an encapsulated driver.

  Mechanically it means canonical_archetype_decl has to become visibility-aware
  — a private archetype only matches within its scope. The semantic layer
  already tracks an exported/private band per decl (semantic.c:5979), so the
  info exists; it just isn't threaded into the codegen-level canonical match
  today. That's a Part 2 detailing item.

  On naming: yes, #module → #plugin is consistent — #module currently means
  "module-private" visibility (visible across a module's files, hidden from
  importers), which is exactly "plugin-private" now. #file stays as-is.

  So my recommendation: allow private archetypes, with private = scope-local 
  identity (no cross-plugin unification), public = today's global structural 
  unification. Does that match your instinct — and do you want all archetypes
  private-by-default (explicit marker to publish into the shared vocabulary), or
  public-by-default (explicit #file/#plugin scope to make one private)?

✻ Cooked for 1m 46s

❯ actually... is plugin the right word? wouldn't you think that a plugin HAS a  
  driver? not that a driver implements plugins?                                 

● You're right to feel the friction — "plugin/driver" fights both words' usual
  meanings, and naming the spine wrong will cost us in the docs forever.

  The mismatch precisely: "plugin" means a part that plugs into a host and 
  extends it, where the host provides the environment. But our "plugin" does the
  opposite — it declares requirements the host must satisfy. It's a
  spec/contract, not an extension. And "driver" means a low-level implementation
  layer, yet we made it the top-level program. So we inverted both. And the
  giveaway: the word that naturally pairs with "driver" isn't "plugin" — it's
  device. You write a driver that implements a device.

  And that hardware metaphor fits this design almost exactly:
  - the .i.arche interface = a datasheet: the shapes/components the thing
  operates on, that you must wire up;
  - the library provides the behavior (systems) — like a device does the actual
  work;
  - writing the program = writing a driver that implements the device from its
  datasheet;
  - one driver supports many devices (one GPU driver, many cards) — matching
  "one driver implements many plugins";
  - and your M2 — "modules that have drivers and are encapsulated" — is
  literally a device that bundles its own driver. You already used the HAS-A
  phrasing.

  So the fix that honors your instinct is: rename "plugin" → "device", keep 
  "driver." Then every sentence reads right: "a device has a driver," "a driver
  implements a device," "a device declares its datasheet (.i.arche); the driver
  provides the concrete data and storage."

  Other coherent vocabularies, if "device" feels too hardware:
  - spec / impl (or interface / implementation) — neutral, accurate, but generic
  and doesn't capture that the library also ships behavior.
  - trait / impl (Rust-flavored) — "a driver impls a trait"; fits "interface +
  default behavior," but "trait" for a whole library is a stretch.

  My recommendation is device / driver — it's the only pairing where both words
  mean what they normally mean, it suits a low-level ECS systems language, and
  the datasheet framing makes the interface file self-explanatory. Which
  vocabulary do you want — device/driver, spec/impl, trait/impl, or keep
  plugin/driver?

● Subagent's back, and it found a decision-relevant collision I'd missed.

  Role A = device, and the .i.arche file = its datasheet. This one's
  unconditional — it's collision-free in the codebase, it nails your HAS-A
  intuition ("a device has a driver"), it makes physics.i.arche literally
  self-explanatory to a systems programmer ("here are the shapes/registers I
  require; here's the behavior I provide"), and M2 names itself ("a device with
  onboard firmware"). Lock that in.

  Role B is the real fork, because of a collision: "driver" reads best on every
  sentence test ("one driver supports many devices," "a device has a driver," M2
  = onboard firmware) — but the word is already taken twice: there's a driver/
  directory (the compiler's own driver, driver/compile.c), and the old
  WORLDS_PLAN.md already uses "driver proc/sys" to mean a lib's test
  scaffolding. So:

  - device / driver — best-reading pair, but you'd have to rename the driver/
  dir (→ compile/ or pipeline/) and retire the old "driver scaffolding" term.
  Small, mechanical refactor.
  - device / host — zero refactoring, no collision, and "host" arguably
  describes "the top-level program" better than "driver" did (a driver is a
  low-level layer; a host is the top of the stack — which is what Role B
  actually is). "A device has a host," "one host drives many devices," M2 =
  "self-hosted device / appliance." This keeps the entire datasheet metaphor
  intact.
  - trait / impl — collision-free and instantly familiar to Rust folks (matches
  @implements ≈ impl … for), but it drops the datasheet metaphor and "impl" is a
  weak noun for the top-level program.

  The subagent's pick: device + datasheet for A no matter what; for B, prefer
  driver if you'll pay the rename, else host.

  My read: if you're not eager to rename the compiler's driver/ directory right
  now, device / host is the sweet spot — same metaphor, zero collision, and
  "host" is honestly more accurate. Which do you want for Role B — driver (with
  the rename), host, or trait/impl?

     ╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
     │ Devices and drivers: libraries expose interfaces, programs implement    │
     │ them                                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Context                                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Arche's archetype/ECS model has one underlying problem: how do a        │
     │ library and the program that uses it share definitional vocabulary —    │
     │ shapes, components/types, and the storage (pools) for them — when the   │
     │ program, not the library, must have the ultimate say, and the two       │
     │ cannot be edited together (e.g. third-party DLLs)?                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The original WORLDS_PLAN.md answered with first-class world values,     │
     │ run/insert/delete … in W, world structs/registries/GEPs, and a          │
     │ @cfg(<slug>) attribute. A long design pass discarded almost all of it   │
     │ for a single spine, using a hardware metaphor:                          │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Everything is a device or a driver — groups all the way up: files →     │
     │ device → driver.                                                        │
     │ - A device (library) is a group of files: a <name>.i.arche datasheet    │
     │ declaring the vocabulary it requires the consumer to define, plus       │
     │ system files providing behavior and a doctest driver. A device exposes  │
     │ an interface and owns no canonical definitions and no storage, so two   │
     │ devices can never collide.                                              │
     │ - A driver (the program/consumer) is a group of devices: it owns the    │
     │ canonical definitions and storage, implements each device's datasheet   │
     │ by binding its own definitions to the requirements (the                 │
     │ @implements(...) decorator), sizes pools, and runs the systems. One     │
     │ driver implements many devices. The top-level program is the driver.    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Why this shape (each point decided during design, grounded in code):    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1. Storage is already canonical-shape-keyed and scope-independent.      │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl / canonical_arch_name (codegen.c:1031-1062)    │
     │ make a name an alias for a shape; get_arch_static_capacity              │
     │ (codegen.c:1065) canonicalizes both sides. No worlds/in W/GEP machinery │
     │ — the only storage gap is naming a shape that lives in another module.  │
     │ 2. @cfg is the wrong primitive — a per-decl attribute clashing with the │
     │ "everything is a group" architecture; its only motivation (test         │
     │ scaffolding) is better served by doctests.                              │
     │ 3. Test scaffolding is already a group: the in-file doctest driver.     │
     │ synthesize() (doctest_run.c:78) prepends the file's entire source and   │
     │ splices an example with its own main at top level (doctest_run.c:84);   │
     │ doctests run only under arche test (cli/cmd_test.c:33), never under     │
     │ arche build. A device cannot be tested as a device — testing it means   │
     │ implementing it, so a device's doctest is a driver: it defines          │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, binds them with               │
     │ @implements(...), sizes pools, and drives the systems. The smallest     │
     │ possible driver, excluded from any real driver's build.                 │
     │ 4. Conflicts must be fixable, so devices own no canonical definitions.  │
     │ A lib-vs-lib clash (two DLLs both defining bar :: int differently) is   │
     │ unfixable by the consumer, so it must never arise. Devices expose       │
     │ requirements; the driver owns canonical defs and the bindings; every    │
     │ error surfaces at the driver, where the consumer can act.               │
     │ 5. Shape/field identity is name-based, and that is correct. bar :: int  │
     │ and baz :: int mean different things; you cannot auto-merge by type     │
     │ without merging health and score. Divergence is resolved by the         │
     │ driver's explicit @implements binding mapping each device's required    │
     │ name onto one canonical definition, type-checked at the bind. Names     │
     │ need not coincide across devices.                                       │
     │ 6. Private by default; the datasheet is the only shared surface. A      │
     │ device's internal types/shapes are normal decls, namespaced to their    │
     │ #file/#plugin scope, never surfaced. Only .i.arche datasheet entries    │
     │ are shared/driver-owned vocabulary.                                     │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The mechanism (datasheet file + @implements decorator)                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/physics.i.arche  — DATASHEET: every decl is a requirement    │
     │ (role carried by the .i.arche name)                                     │
     │ foo :: int                         // a component the driver must own   │
     │ Particle :: archetype { pos, foo } // a shape the driver must provide   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/systems.arche     — device behavior + private decls          │
     │ Scratch :: archetype { tmp }       // private/internal — scoped, never  │
     │ surfaced                                                                │
     │ integrate :: sys { /* uses Particle, foo */ }                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // driver — a group of devices; owns canonical defs; binds with         │
     │ @implements (one decl, many devices)                                    │
     │ #import { physics, render }                                             │
     │ @implements(physics.foo)                                                │
     │ bar :: int                                       // type-checked: int ~ │
     │ int                                                                     │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)                            │
     │ Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }                  // one decl satisfies  │
     │ two devices                                                             │
     │ run physics.integrate;                           // runs against Thing  │
     │ via the binding                                                         │
     │ run render.draw;                                                        │
     │ - The datasheet is a file, not a region: a *.i.arche file in the device │
     │ folder; every decl in it is a requirement. The filename carries the     │
     │ role, consistent with Arche already naming file roles (core.arche,      │
     │ test_*.arche) and discovering modules by glob.                          │
     │ - The binding is a stacked/comma-list @implements(<device>.<req>, …)    │
     │ decorator on the driver's decl, reusing Arche's decorator machinery     │
     │ (@allow/@drop, parser.c:944-1013). The decl is the local side, so       │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle) on Thing means Thing↔Particle. The comma  │
     │ list means one driver type implements many devices at once.             │
     │ - A requirement is typed but name-mapped, not name-matched.             │
     │ - #foreign is the existing precedent (it declares functions a lib       │
     │ requires externally); the .i.arche datasheet rotates that onto          │
     │ types/shapes.                                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Nested composition: M1 now, M2 later                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ For now a device owns nothing canonical and forwards its (and its       │
     │ imports') unsatisfied requirements up to the one root driver — keeping  │
     │ "devices own nothing → no collisions" airtight, one canonical           │
     │ vocabulary at the root. Encapsulated devices-with-their-own-drivers     │
     │ (M2) are a future need, expected to fall out of private scopes +        │
     │ private archetypes (a #file/#plugin region is already a private world)  │
     │ rather than a new mechanism — so build M1 without precluding it.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Standing constraints                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - NEVER move anything to known_failures unless explicitly told. Never   │
     │ touch git. Run make format before tests. Tests under tests/, never      │
     │ tmp/. One test at a time; negative tests for bugs.                      │
     │ - Regression gate: tests/unit/language/systems/ must stay green.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 1 — Ready to build: caller-sized pools + literal unification       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Concrete, file-level, independent — the first deliverables; they stand  │
     │ regardless of how the device/driver system lands.                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1a. Qualified pool decls (driver sizes a device's shape)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Syntax: lib.Particle[1000] (full [C](N){V} grammar), naming an        │
     │ imported shape.                                                         │
     │ - Back end already handles it: import renames a shape to the dotted     │
     │ canonical identity lib.Particle (lower.c prefixed_dup, "%s.%s"); a pool │
     │ decl whose archetype_name is "lib.Particle" resolves via                │
     │ canonical_arch_name and sizes its one global — no codegen change on the │
     │ happy path.                                                             │
     │ - Gap: parse_static_decl (parser.c:757-803) consumes one bare IDENT     │
     │ (line 760) then expects [; lib.Particle[N] bails at the ..              │
     │ - Changes: (1) parser accepts an optional .IDENT chain after the        │
     │ leading IDENT, recording the joined name; (2) lowering carries the      │
     │ dotted name verbatim into archetype_name (confirm hir_q_decl,           │
     │ lower.c:2563, needs no rewrite — it already equals the canonical        │
     │ identity); (3) no-silent-conflict diagnostic in                         │
     │ get_arch_static_capacity (codegen.c:1065) when two pool decls resolve   │
     │ to one canonical shape.                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1b. Anonymous shape literals unify with named shapes                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Goal: arche { foo, bar } lowers to the same canonical shape as a      │
     │ named Foo :: arche { foo, bar }.                                        │
     │ - Current: literals parse (SN_ARCH_EXPR, parser.c:1170); in a binding   │
     │ they lower via lower_archetype_from (lower.c:1666), but an anonymous    │
     │ one in expression position falls through to a placeholder               │
     │ (lower.c:770-775) and never reaches canonical_archetype_decl.           │
     │ - Change: replace the fallthrough so an anonymous SN_ARCH_EXPR mints a  │
     │ synthetic HirArchetypeDecl (deterministic name from the sorted          │
     │ field-name set, so identical literals dedupe), registers it in the      │
     │ program decls, and yields a shape reference — existing field-name       │
     │ canonicalization (archetypes_same_shape, codegen.c:1012) then folds it  │
     │ onto any structurally-identical named shape. No identity-rule change.   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 0 — Prerequisite: free the word "driver"                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ "driver" is currently taken twice: the compiler's own driver/ directory │

     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 2 — Design-stage: the device/driver interface system               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Policy settled (above); mechanics need a focused detailing pass before  │
     │ coding. Captured with code touchpoints:                                 │
     │ - Datasheet *.i.arche (device): extend the module loader                │
     │ (try_load_module_dir / register_module_file, compile.c:114-162) to      │
     │ recognize *.i.arche files in a device folder and register their decls   │
     │ separately, marked "required, not owned" (typed entries — components    │
     │ foo :: int, shapes Particle :: archetype { … }). No new parser syntax;  │
     │ the filename is the marker. Validate that a driver does not re-own a    │
     │ required name except via an @implements bind.                           │
     │ - @implements(<device>.<req>, …) decorator (driver): extend the         │
     │ decorator loop (parser.c:944-1013, alongside @allow/@drop) to recognize │
     │ @implements(...) with a comma list of qualified requirement names;      │
     │ store on the decl like other decorators. The decl is the local side.    │
     │ Produces a per-device name-substitution applied when the device's       │
     │ systems/shapes are lowered into the driver — an extension of the module │
     │ qualify/rename pass (hir_q_decl/hir_rn_decl, lower.c:2320-2563) that    │
     │ already rewrites cross-module names; here it rewrites required names →  │
     │ bound canonical names.                                                  │
     │ - Private archetypes (open sub-decision, lean = allow with scoped       │
     │ identity): today archetype identity is global + structural              │
     │ (canonical_archetype_decl matches by field-name set across the whole    │
     │ program) and import does not prefix field names — so two devices'       │
     │ independent Cache { key, val } would silently share one pool (a         │
     │ hidden-coupling bug the device model makes likely). Fix: make canonical │
     │ matching visibility-aware — public/datasheet shapes unify globally      │
     │ (the feature), private shapes (declared in a #file/#plugin scope) unify │
     │ only within their scope. The semantic exported/private band exists      │
     │ (semantic.c:5979); thread it into the codegen-level match. Open:        │
     │ private-by-default (explicit marker to publish) vs public-by-default    │
     │ (explicit scope to privatize).                                          │
     │ - #module → #plugin rename for the visibility banner (since "module" is │
     │ retired conceptually; #module-private == device-private). #file stays.  │
     │ - Private-by-default: unchanged module prefixing; only .i.arche         │
     │ datasheet entries are shared.                                           │
     │ - Doctest-for-datasheets: a device's doctest is a driver — define       │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, bind with @implements(...),   │
     │ size pools, drive the systems. synthesize() already splices the example │
     │ at top level verbatim, so @implements-decorated decls and pool decls    │
     │ are valid there; confirm the loader makes the device's own .i.arche     │
     │ requirements visible to its doctest.                                    │
     │ - Unsatisfied/incompatible requirements → driver-side error (reuse the  │
     │ sem diagnostic table), naming the requirement and the device — always   │
     │ fixable in the driver.                                                  │
     │ - Entry point: the tuple-group registry is the half-built version of    │
     │ shared vocabulary — g_tgroups[64] (lower.c:1320) is already             │
     │ global/bare-name/unprefixed but lacks conflict handling, cross-module   │
     │ registration (build_tgroups, lower.c:1391, scans only the root), and    │
     │ caps at 64 (register_tgroup, lower.c:1327). Folds into the component    │
     │ side of the datasheet/@implements system.                               │
     │ - Before coding Part 2: write a follow-up pinning the .i.arche          │
     │ datasheet entry rules, the @implements decorator binding/substitution   │
     │ lowering, private-archetype scoping, the component-vs-named-type        │
     │ boundary, and how a device typechecks when built only in a driver's     │
     │ context.                                                                │
     │                                                                         │

     │ - arche init driver <device> — read the device's datasheet, emit a      │
