❯ will archetypes also be in the interface? I'm thinking probably?              

● Yes — and they're arguably the primary interface element. A device's systems
  run over pools of a shape, so for the driver to implement the device it must
  provide a canonical archetype for each shape the systems iterate. The plan's
  datasheet example already carries both kinds of entry:

  // physics/physics.i.arche
  foo :: int                          // a component (atomic vocabulary)
  Particle :: archetype { pos, foo }  // an archetype the systems iterate  ←
  yes, archetypes are in the interface

  So a datasheet has two grains: components (the typed fields) and archetypes
  (the shapes the systems operate on). The @implements(physics.Particle) on the
  driver's Thing is exactly an archetype binding — that's the central case, not
  an edge one.

  The one real consequence to nail down: does the driver's bound archetype have 
  to match the datasheet archetype exactly, or just contain at least its 
  components? The ECS-natural answer is superset — a system over { pos, foo }
  happily runs on a Thing { pos, foo, mass, … } pool, touching only the fields
  it knows. That makes @implements a structural-subtype check (driver shape ⊇
  device requirement), which is more useful than exact-match and matches how
  systems already iterate. I'll record archetypes-in-the-datasheet explicitly
  and flag the exact-vs-superset semantics as the detailing-pass decision.

● Updated plan
  ⎿  /plan to preview
● Recorded: archetypes are explicitly part of the datasheet (with components as
  the finer grain), and the superset / structural-subtype matching semantics for
  @implements archetype binding is flagged as the leaning in Part 2's detailing
  items.
  ⎿  User rejected Claude's plan:
     ╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
     │ Devices and drivers: libraries expose interfaces, programs implement    │
     │ them                                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Context                                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Arche's archetype/ECS model has one underlying problem: how do a        │
     │ library and the program that uses it share definitional vocabulary —    │
     │ shapes, components/types, and the storage (pools) for them — when the   │
     │ program, not the library, must have the ultimate say, and the two       │
     │ cannot be edited together (e.g. third-party DLLs)?                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The original WORLDS_PLAN.md answered with first-class world values,     │
     │ run/insert/delete … in W, world structs/registries/GEPs, and a          │
     │ @cfg(<slug>) attribute. A long design pass discarded almost all of it   │
     │ for a single spine, using a hardware metaphor:                          │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Everything is a device or a driver — groups all the way up: files →     │
     │ device → driver.                                                        │
     │ - A device (library) is a group of files: a <name>.i.arche datasheet    │
     │ declaring the vocabulary it requires the consumer to define, plus       │
     │ system files providing behavior and a doctest driver. A device exposes  │
     │ an interface and owns no canonical definitions and no storage, so two   │
     │ devices can never collide.                                              │
     │ - A driver (the program/consumer) is a group of devices: it owns the    │
     │ canonical definitions and storage, implements each device's datasheet   │
     │ by binding its own definitions to the requirements (the                 │
     │ @implements(...) decorator), sizes pools, and runs the systems. One     │
     │ driver implements many devices. The top-level program is the driver.    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Why this shape (each point decided during design, grounded in code):    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1. Storage is already canonical-shape-keyed and scope-independent.      │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl / canonical_arch_name (codegen.c:1031-1062)    │
     │ make a name an alias for a shape; get_arch_static_capacity              │
     │ (codegen.c:1065) canonicalizes both sides. No worlds/in W/GEP machinery │
     │ — the only storage gap is naming a shape that lives in another module.  │
     │ 2. @cfg is the wrong primitive — a per-decl attribute clashing with the │
     │ "everything is a group" architecture; its only motivation (test         │
     │ scaffolding) is better served by doctests.                              │
     │ 3. Test scaffolding is already a group: the in-file doctest driver.     │
     │ synthesize() (doctest_run.c:78) prepends the file's entire source and   │
     │ splices an example with its own main at top level (doctest_run.c:84);   │
     │ doctests run only under arche test (cli/cmd_test.c:33), never under     │
     │ arche build. A device cannot be tested as a device — testing it means   │
     │ implementing it, so a device's doctest is a driver: it defines          │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, binds them with               │
     │ @implements(...), sizes pools, and drives the systems. The smallest     │
     │ possible driver, excluded from any real driver's build.                 │
     │ 4. Conflicts must be fixable, so devices own no canonical definitions.  │
     │ A lib-vs-lib clash (two DLLs both defining bar :: int differently) is   │
     │ unfixable by the consumer, so it must never arise. Devices expose       │
     │ requirements; the driver owns canonical defs and the bindings; every    │
     │ error surfaces at the driver, where the consumer can act.               │
     │ 5. Shape/field identity is name-based, and that is correct. bar :: int  │
     │ and baz :: int mean different things; you cannot auto-merge by type     │
     │ without merging health and score. Divergence is resolved by the         │
     │ driver's explicit @implements binding mapping each device's required    │
     │ name onto one canonical definition, type-checked at the bind. Names     │
     │ need not coincide across devices.                                       │
     │ 6. Private by default; the datasheet is the only shared surface. A      │
     │ device's internal types/shapes are normal decls, namespaced to their    │
     │ #file/#plugin scope, never surfaced. Only .i.arche datasheet entries    │
     │ are shared/driver-owned vocabulary.                                     │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The mechanism (datasheet file + @implements decorator)                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/physics.i.arche  — DATASHEET: every decl is a requirement    │
     │ (role carried by the .i.arche name)                                     │
     │ foo :: int                         // a component the driver must own   │
     │ Particle :: archetype { pos, foo } // a shape the driver must provide   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/systems.arche     — device behavior + private decls          │
     │ Scratch :: archetype { tmp }       // private/internal — scoped, never  │
     │ surfaced                                                                │
     │ integrate :: sys { /* uses Particle, foo */ }                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // driver — a group of devices; owns canonical defs; binds with         │
     │ @implements (one decl, many devices)                                    │
     │ #import { physics, render }                                             │
     │ @implements(physics.foo)                                                │
     │ bar :: int                                       // type-checked: int ~ │
     │ int                                                                     │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)                            │
     │ Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }                  // one decl satisfies  │
     │ two devices                                                             │
     │ run physics.integrate;                           // runs against Thing  │
     │ via the binding                                                         │
     │ run render.draw;                                                        │
     │ - The datasheet is a file, not a region: a *.i.arche file in the device │
     │ folder; every decl in it is a requirement. The filename carries the     │
     │ role, consistent with Arche already naming file roles (core.arche,      │
     │ test_*.arche) and discovering modules by glob.                          │
     │ - The binding is a stacked/comma-list @implements(<device>.<req>, …)    │
     │ decorator on the driver's decl, reusing Arche's decorator machinery     │
     │ (@allow/@drop, parser.c:944-1013). The decl is the local side, so       │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle) on Thing means Thing↔Particle. The comma  │
     │ list means one driver type implements many devices at once.             │
     │ - A requirement is typed but name-mapped, not name-matched.             │
     │ - #foreign is the existing precedent (it declares functions a lib       │
     │ requires externally); the .i.arche datasheet rotates that onto          │
     │ types/shapes.                                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Nested composition: M1 now, M2 later                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ For now a device owns nothing canonical and forwards its (and its       │
     │ imports') unsatisfied requirements up to the one root driver — keeping  │
     │ "devices own nothing → no collisions" airtight, one canonical           │
     │ vocabulary at the root. Encapsulated devices-with-their-own-drivers     │
     │ (M2) are a future need, expected to fall out of private scopes +        │
     │ private archetypes (a #file/#plugin region is already a private world)  │
     │ rather than a new mechanism — so build M1 without precluding it.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Standing constraints                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - NEVER move anything to known_failures unless explicitly told. Never   │
     │ touch git. Run make format before tests. Tests under tests/, never      │
     │ tmp/. One test at a time; negative tests for bugs.                      │
     │ - Regression gate: tests/unit/language/systems/ must stay green.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 1 — Ready to build: caller-sized pools + literal unification       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Concrete, file-level, independent — the first deliverables; they stand  │
     │ regardless of how the device/driver system lands.                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1a. Qualified pool decls (driver sizes a device's shape)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Syntax: lib.Particle[1000] (full [C](N){V} grammar), naming an        │
     │ imported shape.                                                         │
     │ - Back end already handles it: import renames a shape to the dotted     │
     │ canonical identity lib.Particle (lower.c prefixed_dup, "%s.%s"); a pool │
     │ decl whose archetype_name is "lib.Particle" resolves via                │
     │ canonical_arch_name and sizes its one global — no codegen change on the │
     │ happy path.                                                             │
     │ - Gap: parse_static_decl (parser.c:757-803) consumes one bare IDENT     │
     │ (line 760) then expects [; lib.Particle[N] bails at the ..              │
     │ - Changes: (1) parser accepts an optional .IDENT chain after the        │
     │ leading IDENT, recording the joined name; (2) lowering carries the      │
     │ dotted name verbatim into archetype_name (confirm hir_q_decl,           │
     │ lower.c:2563, needs no rewrite — it already equals the canonical        │
     │ identity); (3) no-silent-conflict diagnostic in                         │
     │ get_arch_static_capacity (codegen.c:1065) when two pool decls resolve   │
     │ to one canonical shape.                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1b. Anonymous shape literals unify with named shapes                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Goal: arche { foo, bar } lowers to the same canonical shape as a      │
     │ named Foo :: arche { foo, bar }.                                        │
     │ - Current: literals parse (SN_ARCH_EXPR, parser.c:1170); in a binding   │
     │ they lower via lower_archetype_from (lower.c:1666), but an anonymous    │
     │ one in expression position falls through to a placeholder               │
     │ (lower.c:770-775) and never reaches canonical_archetype_decl.           │
     │ - Change: replace the fallthrough so an anonymous SN_ARCH_EXPR mints a  │
     │ synthetic HirArchetypeDecl (deterministic name from the sorted          │
     │ field-name set, so identical literals dedupe), registers it in the      │
     │ program decls, and yields a shape reference — existing field-name       │
     │ canonicalization (archetypes_same_shape, codegen.c:1012) then folds it  │
     │ onto any structurally-identical named shape. No identity-rule change.   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 0 — Prerequisite: free the word "driver"                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ "driver" is currently taken twice: the compiler's own driver/ directory │
     │ (driver/compile.c, .h) and the old WORLDS_PLAN.md "driver proc/sys"     │
     │ scaffolding term. Before Part 2's naming lands:                         │
     │ - Rename the driver/ directory → compile/ (pipeline/ alternative);      │
     │ update includes, the build (Makefile/CMake), and references.            │
     │ Mechanical, no behavior change.                                         │
     │ - Retire the old "driver scaffolding" usage (it's superseded by         │
     │ doctest-as-driver here anyway).                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 2 — Design-stage: the device/driver interface system               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Policy settled (above); mechanics need a focused detailing pass before  │
     │ coding. Captured with code touchpoints:                                 │
     │ - Datasheet *.i.arche (device): extend the module loader                │
     │ (try_load_module_dir / register_module_file, compile.c:114-162) to      │
     │ recognize *.i.arche files in a device folder and register their decls   │
     │ separately, marked "required, not owned". A datasheet has two grains,   │
     │ both first-class requirements: components (foo :: int) and archetypes   │
     │ (Particle :: archetype { … }) — the shapes the device's systems         │
     │ iterate, the primary interface element. No new parser syntax; the       │
     │ filename is the marker. Validate that a driver does not re-own a        │
     │ required name except via an @implements bind.                           │
     │ - Archetype binding semantics (open, lean = superset): when a driver's  │
     │ archetype @implements a datasheet archetype, must it match exactly or   │
     │ contain at least the required components? ECS-natural is superset — a   │
     │ system over {pos,foo} runs on a Thing {pos,foo,mass} pool, touching     │
     │ only known fields — making @implements a structural-subtype check       │
     │ (driver shape ⊇ device requirement). Components in the bound shape map  │
     │ by the @implements name correspondence.                                 │
     │ - @implements(<device>.<req>, …) decorator (driver): extend the         │
     │ decorator loop (parser.c:944-1013, alongside @allow/@drop) to recognize │
     │ @implements(...) with a comma list of qualified requirement names;      │
     │ store on the decl like other decorators. The decl is the local side.    │
     │ Produces a per-device name-substitution applied when the device's       │
     │ systems/shapes are lowered into the driver — an extension of the module │
     │ qualify/rename pass (hir_q_decl/hir_rn_decl, lower.c:2320-2563) that    │
     │ already rewrites cross-module names; here it rewrites required names →  │
     │ bound canonical names.                                                  │
     │ - Private archetypes (open sub-decision, lean = allow with scoped       │
     │ identity): today archetype identity is global + structural              │
     │ (canonical_archetype_decl matches by field-name set across the whole    │
     │ program) and import does not prefix field names — so two devices'       │
     │ independent Cache { key, val } would silently share one pool (a         │
     │ hidden-coupling bug the device model makes likely). Fix: make canonical │
     │ matching visibility-aware — public/datasheet shapes unify globally      │
     │ (the feature), private shapes (declared in a #file/#plugin scope) unify │
     │ only within their scope. The semantic exported/private band exists      │
     │ (semantic.c:5979); thread it into the codegen-level match. Open:        │
     │ private-by-default (explicit marker to publish) vs public-by-default    │
     │ (explicit scope to privatize).                                          │
     │ - #module → #plugin rename for the visibility banner (since "module" is │
     │ retired conceptually; #module-private == device-private). #file stays.  │
     │ - Private-by-default: unchanged module prefixing; only .i.arche         │
     │ datasheet entries are shared.                                           │
     │ - Doctest-for-datasheets: a device's doctest is a driver — define       │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, bind with @implements(...),   │
     │ size pools, drive the systems. synthesize() already splices the example │
     │ at top level verbatim, so @implements-decorated decls and pool decls    │
     │ are valid there; confirm the loader makes the device's own .i.arche     │
     │ requirements visible to its doctest.                                    │
     │ - Unsatisfied/incompatible requirements → driver-side error (reuse the  │
     │ sem diagnostic table), naming the requirement and the device — always   │
     │ fixable in the driver.                                                  │
     │ - Entry point: the tuple-group registry is the half-built version of    │
     │ shared vocabulary — g_tgroups[64] (lower.c:1320) is already             │
     │ global/bare-name/unprefixed but lacks conflict handling, cross-module   │
     │ registration (build_tgroups, lower.c:1391, scans only the root), and    │
     │ caps at 64 (register_tgroup, lower.c:1327). Folds into the component    │
     │ side of the datasheet/@implements system.                               │
     │ - Before coding Part 2: write a follow-up pinning the .i.arche          │
     │ datasheet entry rules, the @implements decorator binding/substitution   │
     │ lowering, private-archetype scoping, the component-vs-named-type        │
     │ boundary, and how a device typechecks when built only in a driver's     │
     │ context.                                                                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 3 — Tooling: arche init (driver/device scaffolding)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The datasheet being machine-readable makes scaffolding cheap and        │
     │ operationalizes "what must I define to use this device." A new CLI      │
     │ command beside cmd_test/cmd_build (cli/cmd_init.c):                     │
     │ - arche init driver <device> — read the device's datasheet, emit a      │
     │ driver skeleton: stub canonical defs for each required component/shape, │
     │ an @implements(<device>.<req>) decorator on each, pool-size stubs, and  │
     │ a main that calls the device's systems.                                 │
     │ - arche init device <name> — scaffold a device folder: a .i.arche       │
     │ datasheet, a systems file, and a doctest driver stub that implements    │
     │ the datasheet for arche test.                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Depends on Part 2's datasheet grammar; lands after it.                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 4 — Documentation (the device/driver philosophy is first-class)    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ A core design philosophy, so docs must teach it; each part updates docs │
     │ as it lands. Targets in docs/:                                          │
     │ - New docs/devices.md — the philosophy: "everything is a device or a    │
     │ driver; groups all the way up (files → device → driver); devices expose │
     │ a datasheet and own nothing; drivers implement devices and own the      │
     │ canonical data + storage; why conflicts are driver-side and fixable;    │
     │ the doctest-is-a-driver rule." The conceptual home the rest link to.    │
     │ - docs/language.md — the .i.arche datasheet role, the                   │
     │ @implements(<device>.<req>, …) decorator, qualified pool decls          │

     │ - docs/GRAMMAR.peg — the qualified pool-decl name, the @implements(...) │

     │ - docs/tooling.md — arche init driver/device.                           │
     │ - docs/patterns.md — the device/driver pattern end-to-end;              │
     │ docs/DOCTESTS.md — the doctest-as-driver framing.                       │
     │ - README.md — pointer to docs/devices.md as a headline idea.            │
     │ Retire/redirect WORLDS_PLAN.md.                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 5 — Formatter: decorators on their own line                        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The formatter (cst/format_cst.c) currently inlines decl-level           │
     │ decorators with the decl (it only suppresses the space after @,         │
     │ format_cst.c:95), which is annoying — and bad for stacked               │
     │ @implements(...). Put each decl-level decorator on its own line above   │
     │ the decl. Applies to all decorators                                     │
     │ (@allow/@drop/@intrinsic/@implements), so it lands as a small           │
     │ standalone formatter fix. Refresh formatter goldens; run make format    │
     │ tree-wide and review the mechanical diff.                               │
     │                                                                         │

     │ Explicitly dropped from WORLDS_PLAN                                     │

     │ - The from_import origin bit — deferring devices declare no             │
     │ pools/canonical types; test drivers are doctests excluded from builds.  │
     │ - Lib-vs-lib import-time conflict errors — unfixable; replaced by       │
     │ driver-owned canonical defs + explicit @implements bindings.            │
     │ - Inert HIR_DECL_WORLD / SN_WORLD_DECL / WorldDecl scaffolding stays    │
     │ unused (optional later cleanup).                                        │

     │ Golden: one @lib.Particle global sized 8.                               │
     │ - 1a conflict diagnostic: two pool decls for one shape → new error      │
     │ (negative test).                                                        │
     │ - 1b literal == name: a program referencing a shape by name and by      │

● You're right — I inflated something that's just the definition. The whole
  reason you declare a datasheet is so the device's systems run over the right
  components; a driver naturally provides shapes that contain those components
  (and may have more). There's no "exact vs superset" choice — superset is what
  an interface means here. Let me strip the false fork.

● Updated plan
  ⎿  /plan to preview

● Fixed — it now reads as the definition, not a decision. Re-presenting the
  plan.
  ⎿  User rejected Claude's plan:
     ╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
     │ Devices and drivers: libraries expose interfaces, programs implement    │
     │ them                                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Context                                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Arche's archetype/ECS model has one underlying problem: how do a        │
     │ library and the program that uses it share definitional vocabulary —    │
     │ shapes, components/types, and the storage (pools) for them — when the   │
     │ program, not the library, must have the ultimate say, and the two       │
     │ cannot be edited together (e.g. third-party DLLs)?                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The original WORLDS_PLAN.md answered with first-class world values,     │
     │ run/insert/delete … in W, world structs/registries/GEPs, and a          │
     │ @cfg(<slug>) attribute. A long design pass discarded almost all of it   │
     │ for a single spine, using a hardware metaphor:                          │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Everything is a device or a driver — groups all the way up: files →     │
     │ device → driver.                                                        │
     │ - A device (library) is a group of files: a <name>.i.arche datasheet    │
     │ declaring the vocabulary it requires the consumer to define, plus       │
     │ system files providing behavior and a doctest driver. A device exposes  │
     │ an interface and owns no canonical definitions and no storage, so two   │
     │ devices can never collide.                                              │
     │ - A driver (the program/consumer) is a group of devices: it owns the    │
     │ canonical definitions and storage, implements each device's datasheet   │
     │ by binding its own definitions to the requirements (the                 │
     │ @implements(...) decorator), sizes pools, and runs the systems. One     │
     │ driver implements many devices. The top-level program is the driver.    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Why this shape (each point decided during design, grounded in code):    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1. Storage is already canonical-shape-keyed and scope-independent.      │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl / canonical_arch_name (codegen.c:1031-1062)    │
     │ make a name an alias for a shape; get_arch_static_capacity              │
     │ (codegen.c:1065) canonicalizes both sides. No worlds/in W/GEP machinery │
     │ — the only storage gap is naming a shape that lives in another module.  │
     │ 2. @cfg is the wrong primitive — a per-decl attribute clashing with the │
     │ "everything is a group" architecture; its only motivation (test         │
     │ scaffolding) is better served by doctests.                              │
     │ 3. Test scaffolding is already a group: the in-file doctest driver.     │
     │ synthesize() (doctest_run.c:78) prepends the file's entire source and   │
     │ splices an example with its own main at top level (doctest_run.c:84);   │
     │ doctests run only under arche test (cli/cmd_test.c:33), never under     │
     │ arche build. A device cannot be tested as a device — testing it means   │
     │ implementing it, so a device's doctest is a driver: it defines          │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, binds them with               │
     │ @implements(...), sizes pools, and drives the systems. The smallest     │
     │ possible driver, excluded from any real driver's build.                 │
     │ 4. Conflicts must be fixable, so devices own no canonical definitions.  │
     │ A lib-vs-lib clash (two DLLs both defining bar :: int differently) is   │
     │ unfixable by the consumer, so it must never arise. Devices expose       │
     │ requirements; the driver owns canonical defs and the bindings; every    │
     │ error surfaces at the driver, where the consumer can act.               │
     │ 5. Shape/field identity is name-based, and that is correct. bar :: int  │
     │ and baz :: int mean different things; you cannot auto-merge by type     │
     │ without merging health and score. Divergence is resolved by the         │
     │ driver's explicit @implements binding mapping each device's required    │
     │ name onto one canonical definition, type-checked at the bind. Names     │
     │ need not coincide across devices.                                       │
     │ 6. Private by default; the datasheet is the only shared surface. A      │
     │ device's internal types/shapes are normal decls, namespaced to their    │
     │ #file/#plugin scope, never surfaced. Only .i.arche datasheet entries    │
     │ are shared/driver-owned vocabulary.                                     │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The mechanism (datasheet file + @implements decorator)                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/physics.i.arche  — DATASHEET: every decl is a requirement    │
     │ (role carried by the .i.arche name)                                     │
     │ foo :: int                         // a component the driver must own   │
     │ Particle :: archetype { pos, foo } // a shape the driver must provide   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/systems.arche     — device behavior + private decls          │
     │ Scratch :: archetype { tmp }       // private/internal — scoped, never  │
     │ surfaced                                                                │
     │ integrate :: sys { /* uses Particle, foo */ }                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // driver — a group of devices; owns canonical defs; binds with         │
     │ @implements (one decl, many devices)                                    │
     │ #import { physics, render }                                             │
     │ @implements(physics.foo)                                                │
     │ bar :: int                                       // type-checked: int ~ │
     │ int                                                                     │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)                            │
     │ Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }                  // one decl satisfies  │
     │ two devices                                                             │
     │ run physics.integrate;                           // runs against Thing  │
     │ via the binding                                                         │
     │ run render.draw;                                                        │
     │ - The datasheet is a file, not a region: a *.i.arche file in the device │
     │ folder; every decl in it is a requirement. The filename carries the     │
     │ role, consistent with Arche already naming file roles (core.arche,      │
     │ test_*.arche) and discovering modules by glob.                          │
     │ - The binding is a stacked/comma-list @implements(<device>.<req>, …)    │
     │ decorator on the driver's decl, reusing Arche's decorator machinery     │
     │ (@allow/@drop, parser.c:944-1013). The decl is the local side, so       │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle) on Thing means Thing↔Particle. The comma  │
     │ list means one driver type implements many devices at once.             │
     │ - A requirement is typed but name-mapped, not name-matched.             │
     │ - #foreign is the existing precedent (it declares functions a lib       │
     │ requires externally); the .i.arche datasheet rotates that onto          │
     │ types/shapes.                                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Nested composition: M1 now, M2 later                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ For now a device owns nothing canonical and forwards its (and its       │
     │ imports') unsatisfied requirements up to the one root driver — keeping  │
     │ "devices own nothing → no collisions" airtight, one canonical           │
     │ vocabulary at the root. Encapsulated devices-with-their-own-drivers     │
     │ (M2) are a future need, expected to fall out of private scopes +        │
     │ private archetypes (a #file/#plugin region is already a private world)  │
     │ rather than a new mechanism — so build M1 without precluding it.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Standing constraints                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - NEVER move anything to known_failures unless explicitly told. Never   │
     │ touch git. Run make format before tests. Tests under tests/, never      │
     │ tmp/. One test at a time; negative tests for bugs.                      │
     │ - Regression gate: tests/unit/language/systems/ must stay green.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 1 — Ready to build: caller-sized pools + literal unification       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Concrete, file-level, independent — the first deliverables; they stand  │
     │ regardless of how the device/driver system lands.                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1a. Qualified pool decls (driver sizes a device's shape)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Syntax: lib.Particle[1000] (full [C](N){V} grammar), naming an        │
     │ imported shape.                                                         │
     │ - Back end already handles it: import renames a shape to the dotted     │
     │ canonical identity lib.Particle (lower.c prefixed_dup, "%s.%s"); a pool │
     │ decl whose archetype_name is "lib.Particle" resolves via                │
     │ canonical_arch_name and sizes its one global — no codegen change on the │
     │ happy path.                                                             │
     │ - Gap: parse_static_decl (parser.c:757-803) consumes one bare IDENT     │
     │ (line 760) then expects [; lib.Particle[N] bails at the ..              │
     │ - Changes: (1) parser accepts an optional .IDENT chain after the        │
     │ leading IDENT, recording the joined name; (2) lowering carries the      │
     │ dotted name verbatim into archetype_name (confirm hir_q_decl,           │
     │ lower.c:2563, needs no rewrite — it already equals the canonical        │
     │ identity); (3) no-silent-conflict diagnostic in                         │
     │ get_arch_static_capacity (codegen.c:1065) when two pool decls resolve   │
     │ to one canonical shape.                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1b. Anonymous shape literals unify with named shapes                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Goal: arche { foo, bar } lowers to the same canonical shape as a      │
     │ named Foo :: arche { foo, bar }.                                        │
     │ - Current: literals parse (SN_ARCH_EXPR, parser.c:1170); in a binding   │
     │ they lower via lower_archetype_from (lower.c:1666), but an anonymous    │
     │ one in expression position falls through to a placeholder               │
     │ (lower.c:770-775) and never reaches canonical_archetype_decl.           │
     │ - Change: replace the fallthrough so an anonymous SN_ARCH_EXPR mints a  │
     │ synthetic HirArchetypeDecl (deterministic name from the sorted          │
     │ field-name set, so identical literals dedupe), registers it in the      │
     │ program decls, and yields a shape reference — existing field-name       │
     │ canonicalization (archetypes_same_shape, codegen.c:1012) then folds it  │
     │ onto any structurally-identical named shape. No identity-rule change.   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 0 — Prerequisite: free the word "driver"                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ "driver" is currently taken twice: the compiler's own driver/ directory │
     │ (driver/compile.c, .h) and the old WORLDS_PLAN.md "driver proc/sys"     │
     │ scaffolding term. Before Part 2's naming lands:                         │
     │ - Rename the driver/ directory → compile/ (pipeline/ alternative);      │
     │ update includes, the build (Makefile/CMake), and references.            │
     │ Mechanical, no behavior change.                                         │
     │ - Retire the old "driver scaffolding" usage (it's superseded by         │
     │ doctest-as-driver here anyway).                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 2 — Design-stage: the device/driver interface system               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Policy settled (above); mechanics need a focused detailing pass before  │
     │ coding. Captured with code touchpoints:                                 │
     │ - Datasheet *.i.arche (device): extend the module loader                │
     │ (try_load_module_dir / register_module_file, compile.c:114-162) to      │
     │ recognize *.i.arche files in a device folder and register their decls   │
     │ separately, marked "required, not owned". A datasheet has two grains,   │
     │ both first-class requirements: components (foo :: int) and archetypes   │
     │ (Particle :: archetype { … }) — the shapes the device's systems         │
     │ iterate, the primary interface element. No new parser syntax; the       │
     │ filename is the marker. Validate that a driver does not re-own a        │
     │ required name except via an @implements bind.                           │
     │ - Archetype binding is structural-subtype by definition (not a          │
     │ decision): a datasheet archetype says "the systems need these           │
     │ components"; a driver's archetype satisfies it by containing at least   │
     │ them and may have more — the system only touches what it iterates.      │
     │ @implements checks driver-shape ⊇ device-requirement, components mapped │
     │ by the @implements name correspondence. This is just what defining an   │
     │ interface means.                                                        │
     │ - @implements(<device>.<req>, …) decorator (driver): extend the         │
     │ decorator loop (parser.c:944-1013, alongside @allow/@drop) to recognize │
     │ @implements(...) with a comma list of qualified requirement names;      │
     │ store on the decl like other decorators. The decl is the local side.    │
     │ Produces a per-device name-substitution applied when the device's       │
     │ systems/shapes are lowered into the driver — an extension of the module │
     │ qualify/rename pass (hir_q_decl/hir_rn_decl, lower.c:2320-2563) that    │
     │ already rewrites cross-module names; here it rewrites required names →  │
     │ bound canonical names.                                                  │
     │ - Private archetypes (open sub-decision, lean = allow with scoped       │
     │ identity): today archetype identity is global + structural              │
     │ (canonical_archetype_decl matches by field-name set across the whole    │
     │ program) and import does not prefix field names — so two devices'       │
     │ independent Cache { key, val } would silently share one pool (a         │
     │ hidden-coupling bug the device model makes likely). Fix: make canonical │
     │ matching visibility-aware — public/datasheet shapes unify globally      │
     │ (the feature), private shapes (declared in a #file/#plugin scope) unify │
     │ only within their scope. The semantic exported/private band exists      │
     │ (semantic.c:5979); thread it into the codegen-level match. Open:        │
     │ private-by-default (explicit marker to publish) vs public-by-default    │
     │ (explicit scope to privatize).                                          │
     │ - #module → #plugin rename for the visibility banner (since "module" is │
     │ retired conceptually; #module-private == device-private). #file stays.  │
     │ - Private-by-default: unchanged module prefixing; only .i.arche         │
     │ datasheet entries are shared.                                           │
     │ - Doctest-for-datasheets: a device's doctest is a driver — define       │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, bind with @implements(...),   │
     │ size pools, drive the systems. synthesize() already splices the example │
     │ at top level verbatim, so @implements-decorated decls and pool decls    │
     │ are valid there; confirm the loader makes the device's own .i.arche     │
     │ requirements visible to its doctest.                                    │
     │ - Unsatisfied/incompatible requirements → driver-side error (reuse the  │
     │ sem diagnostic table), naming the requirement and the device — always   │
     │ fixable in the driver.                                                  │
     │ - Entry point: the tuple-group registry is the half-built version of    │
     │ shared vocabulary — g_tgroups[64] (lower.c:1320) is already             │
     │ global/bare-name/unprefixed but lacks conflict handling, cross-module   │
     │ registration (build_tgroups, lower.c:1391, scans only the root), and    │
     │ caps at 64 (register_tgroup, lower.c:1327). Folds into the component    │
     │ side of the datasheet/@implements system.                               │
     │ - Before coding Part 2: write a follow-up pinning the .i.arche          │
     │ datasheet entry rules, the @implements decorator binding/substitution   │
     │ lowering, private-archetype scoping, the component-vs-named-type        │
     │ boundary, and how a device typechecks when built only in a driver's     │
     │ context.                                                                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 3 — Tooling: arche init (driver/device scaffolding)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The datasheet being machine-readable makes scaffolding cheap and        │
     │ operationalizes "what must I define to use this device." A new CLI      │
     │ command beside cmd_test/cmd_build (cli/cmd_init.c):                     │
     │ - arche init driver <device> — read the device's datasheet, emit a      │
     │ driver skeleton: stub canonical defs for each required component/shape, │
     │ an @implements(<device>.<req>) decorator on each, pool-size stubs, and  │
     │ a main that calls the device's systems.                                 │
     │ - arche init device <name> — scaffold a device folder: a .i.arche       │
     │ datasheet, a systems file, and a doctest driver stub that implements    │
     │ the datasheet for arche test.                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Depends on Part 2's datasheet grammar; lands after it.                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 4 — Documentation (the device/driver philosophy is first-class)    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ A core design philosophy, so docs must teach it; each part updates docs │
     │ as it lands. Targets in docs/:                                          │
     │ - New docs/devices.md — the philosophy: "everything is a device or a    │
     │ driver; groups all the way up (files → device → driver); devices expose │
     │ a datasheet and own nothing; drivers implement devices and own the      │
     │ canonical data + storage; why conflicts are driver-side and fixable;    │
     │ the doctest-is-a-driver rule." The conceptual home the rest link to.    │
     │ - docs/language.md — the .i.arche datasheet role, the                   │
     │ @implements(<device>.<req>, …) decorator, qualified pool decls          │
     │ (lib.Particle[N]), anonymous shape literals / structural shape          │
     │ identity, public-vs-private shapes.                                     │
     │ - docs/GRAMMAR.peg — the qualified pool-decl name, the @implements(...) │
     │ decorator, anonymous-literal positions (kept in sync with the parser).  │
     │ - docs/tooling.md — arche init driver/device.                           │
     │ - docs/patterns.md — the device/driver pattern end-to-end;              │
     │ docs/DOCTESTS.md — the doctest-as-driver framing.                       │
     │ - README.md — pointer to docs/devices.md as a headline idea.            │
     │ Retire/redirect WORLDS_PLAN.md.                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 5 — Formatter: decorators on their own line                        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The formatter (cst/format_cst.c) currently inlines decl-level           │
     │ decorators with the decl (it only suppresses the space after @,         │
     │ format_cst.c:95), which is annoying — and bad for stacked               │
     │ @implements(...). Put each decl-level decorator on its own line above   │
     │ the decl. Applies to all decorators                                     │
     │ (@allow/@drop/@intrinsic/@implements), so it lands as a small           │
     │ standalone formatter fix. Refresh formatter goldens; run make format    │
     │ tree-wide and review the mechanical diff.                               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Explicitly dropped from WORLDS_PLAN                                     │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - world decls, run/insert/delete … in W, world struct/registry/GEPs.    │
     │ - @cfg(<slug>) and flag-dependent compilation — replaced by doctest     │
     │ drivers.                                                                │
     │ - The from_import origin bit — deferring devices declare no             │
     │ pools/canonical types; test drivers are doctests excluded from builds.  │
     │ - Lib-vs-lib import-time conflict errors — unfixable; replaced by       │
     │ driver-owned canonical defs + explicit @implements bindings.            │
     │ - Inert HIR_DECL_WORLD / SN_WORLD_DECL / WorldDecl scaffolding stays    │
     │ unused (optional later cleanup).                                        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Verification                                                            │
     │                                                                         │
     │ make format, then the lit harness under tests/unit/language/ (with      │
     │ systems//pool tests):                                                   │
     │ - 1a import + size: device (shape + integrate :: sys, no pool) imported │
     │ by a driver writing lib.Particle[8], inserts, runs, reads back.         │
     │ Golden: one @lib.Particle global sized 8.                               │
     │ - 1a conflict diagnostic: two pool decls for one shape → new error      │
     │ (negative test).                                                        │
     │ - 1b literal == name: a program referencing a shape by name and by      │
     │ arche {foo,bar} → golden shows one shared %struct/global; IR identical  │
     │ to the name-only equivalent.                                            │
     │ - Doctest driver: doctest in the device file supplies its own pool/defs │
     │ and drives the system → arche test <device> passes; absent from a       │
     │ driver's arche build IR.                                                │
     │ - Bare unaffected: existing single-file Particle[N] program             │
     │ byte-identical. Regression gate tests/unit/language/systems/ green.     │
     │ - Part 0: compiler builds + full test suite green after the             │
     │ driver/→compile/ rename (pure refactor).                                │
     │ - Part 2: verification in its follow-up (notably: an @implements rebind │
     │ produces correct shared canonical storage; two devices' private         │
     │ same-shape archetypes get distinct pools; unsatisfied requirement       │
     │ errors at the driver; the formatter puts @implements on its own line).  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Backward compatibility                                                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Part 1 is additive — bare Name[...] pool decls, single-file programs,   │
     │ and existing IR unchanged; new surface is an optional .-qualified pool  │
     │ name and functional anonymous arche {...} literals. Part 0 is a pure    │
     │ rename. Part 2 adds the .i.arche datasheet role and the                 │
     │ @implements(...) decorator, used by no existing program, and must keep  │
     │ single-module programs and tests/unit/language/systems/ byte-identical. │

● Threaded through: archetypes are global-only for now (parser/semantic rejects
  an archetype decl in any nested scope), all in the one structural-canonical
  namespace the root driver owns; visibility-aware matching and private shapes
  are explicitly deferred to M2. The example, point 6, Part 2, docs, and

     ╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
     │ Devices and drivers: libraries expose interfaces, programs implement    │
     │ them                                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Context                                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Arche's archetype/ECS model has one underlying problem: how do a        │
     │ library and the program that uses it share definitional vocabulary —    │
     │ shapes, components/types, and the storage (pools) for them — when the   │
     │ program, not the library, must have the ultimate say, and the two       │
     │ cannot be edited together (e.g. third-party DLLs)?                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The original WORLDS_PLAN.md answered with first-class world values,     │
     │ run/insert/delete … in W, world structs/registries/GEPs, and a          │
     │ @cfg(<slug>) attribute. A long design pass discarded almost all of it   │
     │ for a single spine, using a hardware metaphor:                          │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Everything is a device or a driver — groups all the way up: files →     │
     │ device → driver.                                                        │
     │ - A device (library) is a group of files: a <name>.i.arche datasheet    │
     │ declaring the vocabulary it requires the consumer to define, plus       │
     │ system files providing behavior and a doctest driver. A device exposes  │
     │ an interface and owns no canonical definitions and no storage, so two   │
     │ devices can never collide.                                              │
     │ - A driver (the program/consumer) is a group of devices: it owns the    │
     │ canonical definitions and storage, implements each device's datasheet   │
     │ by binding its own definitions to the requirements (the                 │
     │ @implements(...) decorator), sizes pools, and runs the systems. One     │
     │ driver implements many devices. The top-level program is the driver.    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Why this shape (each point decided during design, grounded in code):    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1. Storage is already canonical-shape-keyed and scope-independent.      │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl / canonical_arch_name (codegen.c:1031-1062)    │
     │ make a name an alias for a shape; get_arch_static_capacity              │
     │ (codegen.c:1065) canonicalizes both sides. No worlds/in W/GEP machinery │
     │ — the only storage gap is naming a shape that lives in another module.  │
     │ 2. @cfg is the wrong primitive — a per-decl attribute clashing with the │
     │ "everything is a group" architecture; its only motivation (test         │
     │ scaffolding) is better served by doctests.                              │
     │ 3. Test scaffolding is already a group: the in-file doctest driver.     │
     │ synthesize() (doctest_run.c:78) prepends the file's entire source and   │
     │ splices an example with its own main at top level (doctest_run.c:84);   │
     │ doctests run only under arche test (cli/cmd_test.c:33), never under     │
     │ arche build. A device cannot be tested as a device — testing it means   │
     │ implementing it, so a device's doctest is a driver: it defines          │
     │ canonical types satisfying the datasheet, binds them with               │
     │ @implements(...), sizes pools, and drives the systems. The smallest     │
     │ possible driver, excluded from any real driver's build.                 │
     │ 4. Conflicts must be fixable, so devices own no canonical definitions.  │
     │ A lib-vs-lib clash (two DLLs both defining bar :: int differently) is   │
     │ unfixable by the consumer, so it must never arise. Devices expose       │
     │ requirements; the driver owns canonical defs and the bindings; every    │
     │ error surfaces at the driver, where the consumer can act.               │
     │ 5. Shape/field identity is name-based, and that is correct. bar :: int  │
     │ and baz :: int mean different things; you cannot auto-merge by type     │
     │ without merging health and score. Divergence is resolved by the         │
     │ driver's explicit @implements binding mapping each device's required    │
     │ name onto one canonical definition, type-checked at the bind. Names     │
     │ need not coincide across devices.                                       │
     │ 6. Archetypes are global; non-archetype internals are private. For now  │
     │ archetypes may be declared only at global scope — they form one global  │
     │ structural-canonical namespace, the shared vocabulary the driver owns   │
     │ (scoped/private archetypes are deferred to M2). A device's              │
     │ non-archetype internals (type aliases, procs, systems) stay             │
     │ namespaced/private to their #file/#plugin scope; only .i.arche          │
     │ datasheet entries are the device's shared surface.                      │
     │                                                                         │
     │ The mechanism (datasheet file + @implements decorator)                  │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/physics.i.arche  — DATASHEET: every decl is a requirement    │
     │ (role carried by the .i.arche name)                                     │
     │ foo :: int                         // a component the driver must own   │
     │ Particle :: archetype { pos, foo } // a shape the driver must provide   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // physics/systems.arche     — device behavior (archetypes are global;  │
     │ the device owns none)                                                   │
     │ integrate :: sys { /* uses the datasheet's Particle / foo, provided by  │
     │ the driver */ }                                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ // driver — a group of devices; owns canonical defs; binds with         │
     │ @implements (one decl, many devices)                                    │
     │ #import { physics, render }                                             │
     │ @implements(physics.foo)                                                │
     │ bar :: int                                       // type-checked: int ~ │
     │ int                                                                     │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle, render.Sprite)                            │
     │ Thing :: archetype { pos, bar }                  // one decl satisfies  │
     │ two devices                                                             │
     │ run physics.integrate;                           // runs against Thing  │
     │ via the binding                                                         │
     │ run render.draw;                                                        │
     │ - The datasheet is a file, not a region: a *.i.arche file in the device │
     │ folder; every decl in it is a requirement. The filename carries the     │
     │ role, consistent with Arche already naming file roles (core.arche,      │
     │ test_*.arche) and discovering modules by glob.                          │
     │ - The binding is a stacked/comma-list @implements(<device>.<req>, …)    │
     │ decorator on the driver's decl, reusing Arche's decorator machinery     │
     │ (@allow/@drop, parser.c:944-1013). The decl is the local side, so       │
     │ @implements(physics.Particle) on Thing means Thing↔Particle. The comma  │
     │ list means one driver type implements many devices at once.             │
     │ - A requirement is typed but name-mapped, not name-matched.             │
     │ - #foreign is the existing precedent (it declares functions a lib       │
     │ requires externally); the .i.arche datasheet rotates that onto          │
     │ types/shapes.                                                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Nested composition: M1 now, M2 later                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ For now a device owns nothing canonical and forwards its (and its       │
     │ imports') unsatisfied requirements up to the one root driver — keeping  │
     │ "devices own nothing → no collisions" airtight, one canonical           │
     │ vocabulary at the root. Encapsulated devices-with-their-own-drivers     │
     │ (M2) are a future need, expected to fall out of private scopes +        │
     │ private archetypes (a #file/#plugin region is already a private world)  │
     │ rather than a new mechanism — so build M1 without precluding it.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Standing constraints                                                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - NEVER move anything to known_failures unless explicitly told. Never   │
     │ touch git. Run make format before tests. Tests under tests/, never      │
     │ tmp/. One test at a time; negative tests for bugs.                      │
     │ - Regression gate: tests/unit/language/systems/ must stay green.        │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 1 — Ready to build: caller-sized pools + literal unification       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Concrete, file-level, independent — the first deliverables; they stand  │
     │ regardless of how the device/driver system lands.                       │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1a. Qualified pool decls (driver sizes a device's shape)                │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Syntax: lib.Particle[1000] (full [C](N){V} grammar), naming an        │
     │ imported shape.                                                         │
     │ - Back end already handles it: import renames a shape to the dotted     │
     │ canonical identity lib.Particle (lower.c prefixed_dup, "%s.%s"); a pool │
     │ decl whose archetype_name is "lib.Particle" resolves via                │
     │ canonical_arch_name and sizes its one global — no codegen change on the │
     │ happy path.                                                             │
     │ - Gap: parse_static_decl (parser.c:757-803) consumes one bare IDENT     │
     │ (line 760) then expects [; lib.Particle[N] bails at the ..              │
     │ - Changes: (1) parser accepts an optional .IDENT chain after the        │
     │ leading IDENT, recording the joined name; (2) lowering carries the      │
     │ dotted name verbatim into archetype_name (confirm hir_q_decl,           │
     │ lower.c:2563, needs no rewrite — it already equals the canonical        │
     │ identity); (3) no-silent-conflict diagnostic in                         │
     │ get_arch_static_capacity (codegen.c:1065) when two pool decls resolve   │
     │ to one canonical shape.                                                 │
     │                                                                         │
     │ 1b. Anonymous shape literals unify with named shapes                    │
     │                                                                         │
     │ - Goal: arche { foo, bar } lowers to the same canonical shape as a      │
     │ named Foo :: arche { foo, bar }.                                        │
     │ - Current: literals parse (SN_ARCH_EXPR, parser.c:1170); in a binding   │
     │ they lower via lower_archetype_from (lower.c:1666), but an anonymous    │
     │ one in expression position falls through to a placeholder               │
     │ (lower.c:770-775) and never reaches canonical_archetype_decl.           │
     │ - Change: replace the fallthrough so an anonymous SN_ARCH_EXPR mints a  │
     │ synthetic HirArchetypeDecl (deterministic name from the sorted          │
     │ field-name set, so identical literals dedupe), registers it in the      │
     │ program decls, and yields a shape reference — existing field-name       │
     │ canonicalization (archetypes_same_shape, codegen.c:1012) then folds it  │
     │ onto any structurally-identical named shape. No identity-rule change.   │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 0 — Prerequisite: free the word "driver"                           │
     │                                                                         │
     │ "driver" is currently taken twice: the compiler's own driver/ directory │
     │ (driver/compile.c, .h) and the old WORLDS_PLAN.md "driver proc/sys"     │
     │ scaffolding term. Before Part 2's naming lands:                         │
     │ - Rename the driver/ directory → compile/ (pipeline/ alternative);      │
     │ update includes, the build (Makefile/CMake), and references.            │
     │ Mechanical, no behavior change.                                         │
     │ - Retire the old "driver scaffolding" usage (it's superseded by         │
     │ doctest-as-driver here anyway).                                         │
     │                                                                         │
     │ ---                                                                     │
     │ Part 2 — Design-stage: the device/driver interface system               │
     │                                                                         │
     │ Policy settled (above); mechanics need a focused detailing pass before  │
     │ coding. Captured with code touchpoints:                                 │
     │ - Datasheet *.i.arche (device): extend the module loader                │
     │ (try_load_module_dir / register_module_file, compile.c:114-162) to      │
     │ recognize *.i.arche files in a device folder and register their decls   │
     │ separately, marked "required, not owned". A datasheet has two grains,   │
     │ both first-class requirements: components (foo :: int) and archetypes   │
     │ (Particle :: archetype { … }) — the shapes the device's systems         │
     │ iterate, the primary interface element. No new parser syntax; the       │
     │ filename is the marker. Validate that a driver does not re-own a        │
     │ required name except via an @implements bind.                           │
     │ - Archetype binding is structural-subtype by definition (not a          │
     │ decision): a datasheet archetype says "the systems need these           │
     │ components"; a driver's archetype satisfies it by containing at least   │
     │ them and may have more — the system only touches what it iterates.      │
     │ @implements checks driver-shape ⊇ device-requirement, components mapped │
     │ by the @implements name correspondence. This is just what defining an   │
     │ interface means.                                                        │
     │ - @implements(<device>.<req>, …) decorator (driver): extend the         │
     │ decorator loop (parser.c:944-1013, alongside @allow/@drop) to recognize │
     │ @implements(...) with a comma list of qualified requirement names;      │
     │ store on the decl like other decorators. The decl is the local side.    │
     │ Produces a per-device name-substitution applied when the device's       │
     │ systems/shapes are lowered into the driver — an extension of the module │
     │ qualify/rename pass (hir_q_decl/hir_rn_decl, lower.c:2320-2563) that    │
     │ already rewrites cross-module names; here it rewrites required names →  │
     │ bound canonical names.                                                  │
     │ - Archetypes are global-only for now (private archetypes deferred):     │
     │ permit archetype decls only at global scope; the parser/semantic        │
     │ rejects an archetype decl nested inside a #file/#plugin/block scope.    │
     │ All archetypes stay in the one global structural-canonical namespace —  │
     │ canonical_archetype_decl (codegen.c:1031) is unchanged.                 │
     │ Visibility-aware canonical matching and per-device private shapes are a │

     │ - #module → #plugin rename for the visibility banner (since "module" is │

     │ - Doctest-for-datasheets: a device's doctest is a driver — define       │

     │ rename. Part 2 adds the .i.arche datasheet role and the                 │

● Good question, and there's a clean principled line through it — storage.

  - Archetypes carry storage (pools). A device owns no storage, so a device
  never declares a private/owned archetype — it only references archetypes
  through its datasheet (requirements the driver provides). That's already
  settled by the global-only rule: no archetypes in a device outside its
  interface, period.
  - Non-archetype types are storage-free (a Quat alias, a small struct, an enum
  — just a layout for values, no pool). So a device can hold these as private 
  internals, namespaced (lib.Quat), used inside its systems, never shared and
  never collidable. They don't make the device own storage, so they don't break
  the model.

  The boundary between "private internal" and "must be in the datasheet" then
  falls out automatically: a type that appears in the interface — a datasheet
  archetype's field type, or a type in a system signature the driver calls — has
  to be in the datasheet (the driver must know it). A type used only inside a 
  system body stays private. So:

  ▎ The datasheet contains what crosses the device↔driver boundary 
  ▎ (storage-bearing archetypes + any types named in the interface). 
  ▎ Storage-free internals stay private in the device.

  So my answer to "types/archetypes outside the interface": archetypes — no; 
  private non-archetype types — yes. That keeps "devices own no storage" exact
  while letting systems have their own internal type vocabulary.

  Is that the split you want — or do you want M1 stricter (datasheet + systems
  only, no private type decls at all in a device)? If the storage-based split is
  right, I'll record it in the plan.

✻ Sautéed for 4m 18s
